Jinan Football Zhenru Basketball Team's Philippine Campaign Record (11)

(Reported by our reporter Wen Chu from Manila on February 2nd)

The Jinan Football Team and Zhenru Basketball Team's campaign in the Philippines has come to a successful conclusion. This campaign has opened up unprecedented honors for Chinese football in the Philippines (Nanhua and Lehua's victories are comparable, but not total victories). The athletes are about to set sail northward, all filled with joy. In the future, Zhenru's solemn and magnificent hall will surely hold a grand celebration, and the Huangpu River will also play the triumphant song. The reporter regrets not being able to attend the grand occasion in person, and can only write about the events before and after this event, as well as the details of the sports arena, and publish them in the newspaper as conversation starters for the welcome meeting.

▲I'll Show My Ugly Merits

The Zhenru football team played five games. The first game was against La Salle University, which was 3 to 3. The second game was against San Beda University, which was 3 to 2. The third game was against Santo Tomas University, which was 4 to 1. The fourth game was against the All-Nations United Team, which was 3 to 1. The fifth game was against the All-Philippine All-Star Team, which was 2 to 1 (although it was not completed because the audience caused trouble, but there were only five or six minutes left, so it was considered a victory). In terms of individual achievements, Chen Zhenhe scored a total of eight goals, Dai Linjing scored a total of six goals, Chen Jiaqiu scored one goal, and Luo Haiguang scored one goal. However, this victory was due to the coordination and support of all the players. Those in the front are naturally responsible for charging and breaking through, and those in the back are naturally responsible for clearing the invading enemy troops. The strength of the All-Nations Team and the All-Star Team is actually not to be underestimated. The defeat was due to everyone vying to make contributions and show off their own skills, so they ultimately achieved nothing.

▲Overseas Chinese Provide Great Support

The support of the overseas Chinese this time can be said to be extremely enthusiastic. The four Chinese newspapers unanimously did their best to promote and publicize the victory. When they won, they rushed to publish special editions to allow the general overseas Chinese to see the good news as soon as possible. At this time of expensive gold and cheap silver, and with sluggish business, the Philippine peso can be exchanged for more than two yuan in national currency and sent back to the motherland to comfort relatives and friends. How passionate! Even the most frugal and hardworking laborers spared three or two yuan, intending to cheer and show their usual accumulated national humiliation.

▲Entrance Ticket Revenue

The purpose of the Charity Association is to focus on the overseas Chinese aspect of the entrance ticket revenue. The more the motherland's team wins, the more enthusiastic the overseas Chinese will be to visit. In the first game, the revenue was only more than two thousand yuan. The result of the game was also a tie. It is said that the general manager Liu Qinggao looked worried and said that if the visiting team lost again, the revenue would be greatly affected, or even insufficient to cover expenses. Now it is very promising. According to Ying's announcement, the revenue from five basketball games was more than six thousand yuan, and the revenue from four football games was 21,000 yuan (the final game has not yet been announced). The total must be more than 30,000 yuan. The travel expenses, accommodation, venue arrangement fees, advertising and publicity fees, etc. for this trip for the athletes are only 15,000 yuan. This method of raising funds can be said to not require door-to-door begging. Everyone actively contributes. There were also Japanese martial arts fighters, but the entrance ticket revenue was not detailed because it was not paid attention to.

▲British and Americans Predict

After the first two games, British and Americans with sports knowledge said that the Jinan team would win. The reason is that they have a spirit of cooperation and the formation is not chaotic from beginning to end. Every time they serve, there is a response. Therefore, those who bet on the outcome all favored the Jinan team (that is, those who favored Jinan accounted for a clear majority over a minority).

▲Contacting Emotions?

In 1925, the Far Eastern Games were held in Manila, and there was a disturbance between the Chinese and Philippine football teams. In 1927, the Lehua football team also had a dispute with San Beda (the players who were defeated started to hit our players, they said they would not go, and the public opinion strongly attacked them). This time, the reporter was fortunate to have a complete result. However, even in the last few minutes, it was difficult to avoid an unfortunate fact. Although it did not harm the honor of the entire team, it also left a crack in the history of Chinese and Philippine sports. Please see the following interesting things to know that the disturbance was unavoidable.

▲Eating Porridge and Drinking Water

In the crowd, it is very appropriate to applaud and cheer as a proper way to cheer. However, every time the opposing team wins, the Filipinos must shout "eat porridge." This is because overseas Chinese are accustomed to eating porridge for breakfast and dinner, mocking us for being weak from eating porridge. If our team wins, the crowd shouts "drink water" to retaliate. Filipinos use water instead of tea, mocking them for being soft on water. Similar mutual ridicule and disagreements can lead to fights everywhere. Therefore, it can be said that international sports increase sports interest, improve sports standards, and express the national spirit of each country. However, if it is said to enhance the relationship between the two countries, it is actually the opposite between China and the Philippines.

▲Ashamed of Our Guests

This time, the sports event was not between the local overseas Chinese team and them at will. It was specially invited by the highest academic institution in our country, the championship team, to travel thousands of miles to create a scene for their charity association. However, the audience dared to insult our on-site staff, so it is no wonder that the overseas Chinese were embarrassed. The police also wanted to arrest our athletes, which was even more unreasonable. Fortunately, the people from the Charity Association ran around to mediate, and the city referee did not want to pursue the matter deeply. The police station's desire to prosecute and release the two Chinese was also withdrawn. I hope that from now on, the clouds will clear and the past will be forgotten.

▲Fortunately, All Athletes

During these three weeks, everyone in the streets and alleys talked about the victory in the stadium. Compared with the tens of thousands of tons of warships sent by the motherland parked in Manila Bay, it was even more animated. The prestigious names of Dai Linjing, Chen Zhenhe, Ming Taizu, Long-legged Immortal, etc., left a deeper impression on the overseas Chinese community than the visits of great men and the rich. I hope that the future athletes will rise up quickly. Warships and airplanes cannot be built in a short time. The only way to increase international honor for the motherland now is in the sports arena with the good skills of the athletes.

▲Special Respect

This victory is due to the efforts of every player. I have said it many times. However, there are a few people who should be given even more respect. Dai Linjing is the general staff and the dispatcher is appropriate, and the command is satisfactory. He is the reincarnation of Zhao Zilong, the victorious general of Changshan. Chen Zhenhe took the lead and was brave in charging, scaring the enemy with one foot. He is the younger brother of Guan Yu, Zhang Yide, the iron-faced general. Zhuang Shanhong firmly defends the center and coordinates effectively, and is as majestic as the Dharma protector Weituo. Feng Yunyou and Jiang Shanjing are bronze-footed and iron-headed, and defend the inner guards like the iron gate gods Shen Tu and Yu Lei. With them in their seats, ghosts dare not peep at the door. The remaining titles can remain the same.

▲Five Years and Ten Years

Someone familiar with the situation in China and the Philippines and who has a long-standing interest in sports told me that more than half of the Philippine athletes come from poor families and have reddish-brown skin, purely of Malay ethnicity, and have unattractive faces. For example, the basketball star Jacinto is like the son of Lai in the shadow play Fire Burning Red Lotus Temple. These athletes can be guaranteed to exercise their bodies for a long time in ten years without external temptations. If our athletes are all spirited, and now the communication between men and women in various universities is open, many queens, palace masters and school flowers are more willing to be close to the athletes who are welcomed by all in the sports arena. So in Chen Zhang'e's Philippine diary, he wrote that the tears of many lovers were seen off in the spring river as an embellishment for the journey. Then, the beauty will naturally be long and the heroes will be short. I don’t have to argue about whether someone’s words are true or reasonable. I only hope that all the athletes will maintain this indestructible body and be the pillars of the motherland. Don’t be like a ball that can’t roll out of the net once it enters the city.

▲The Whole Team Stays for Ten Days

One more thing to tell the readers: all the athletes were originally scheduled to return home today, but the fight case has been canceled and the carnival will open tonight. The Charity Association again pleaded to stay for ten days, and there will be several friendly football and basketball games. I will extend the happy brush and announce the future situation to you.

Free Talk

Words of Wisdom·Xu Jie·

Many doors, many headaches. Many words, many things.

▲Circumstances are like writing an essay. A good essay cannot only have smooth strokes and no difficult strokes. Life should not only have smooth circumstances and no adversity.

▲Children are the decorations in front of the spirit altar a hundred years later.

▲Qi is the most important thing in life. As the saying goes, "Qi and strength." This is because there is strength only when there is Qi. As the saying goes, "Integrity." This is because there is integrity only when there is Qi. The Buddha said, "Life is between breaths." One does not die if one does not eat for a day, but one dies without Qi for a moment. How can the people of the world be dreamy, depressed and constipated, angry and hurt their Qi, and happy and consume their Qi, and only use medicinal stones for nourishment without following the ways of "nourishing Qi" and "taking Qi"? What is the use?

▲Water that is too clear has no fish. Crazy people declare that they are not in harmony with the world. Zhou Maoshu praised the lotus flower for emerging from the mud without being stained. This is indeed the way for a gentleman to conduct himself in the world.

▲I love the poems of Fang Weng and Yao Fu the most. Fang Weng's poem says, "Fang Weng does not care about the affairs of the world. The taste of sleep is infinitely sweet like honey." This is a good sleeping pill. Yao Fu's poem says, "Yao Fu is not fond of chanting poetry. Poetry is when Yao Fu is happy. Clearly dressed as a scholar. Talking about benevolence and righteousness as a man. Dare to open his eyes in the world. Willing to frown in the world. Sixty-seven years of uneventful days. Yao Fu is not fond of chanting poetry." When my father was alive, he loved to chant this poem. But now I can't hear it anymore. How painful!

Recording the Loss of Our Nation's Books and Records – Qing Qu

The flourishing of our nation's books and records began with stone inscriptions, followed by woodblock printing, and lastly movable type (invented by Bi Sheng, a commoner of the Song Dynasty). However, as the script transitioned from seal to clerical, from complex to simplified, from bamboo slips to paper, and with the rise of printing, books became more numerous, and readers began to take them less seriously. This is simply a sign of the times. Ye Mengde said, "Today, the best books are printed in Hangzhou, followed by Sichuan, and the worst in Fujian." This gives us a glimpse of the state of book publishing in the Song Dynasty.

Leaving aside older examples, rare and secret books from the Song Dynasty are the most highly prized. Even during the Yongle era of the Ming Dynasty, only 30% of the books stored in the Wenyuan Pavilion were block-printed, with the remaining 70% being handwritten copies. This shows the limited extent of woodblock printing at that time. By the Wanli era, when an imperial decree was issued to collate the remaining books, only local gazetteers remained, with few classical texts surviving. This is why Song Dynasty printings are so highly valued. This year, the China Science Society held a book exhibition at the Mingfu Library on January 1st, displaying dozens of Northern Song Dynasty printed scriptures and Sui and Tang Dynasty handwritten scriptures, astonishing those who saw them. The society's efforts to promote national culture and collect scattered remnants are truly commendable.

This reminds me of the Japanese reprints of ancient script versions of the Classic of Filial Piety and the Book of Documents, which are among our nation's oldest books. I wonder how they ended up in Japan. Furthermore, the Library of Congress in the United States holds over 1,700 types of Chinese books, totaling approximately 20,000 volumes, mostly consisting of collected works and private writings. These are recent exports. If we include previous exports, the total would be no less than 125,000 volumes, a truly astonishing figure. Some may not believe it, but news agencies like the World News Agency and the National News Agency have reported it clearly and authoritatively, not based on hearsay.

Red Mud Splatters the City of Paris – Lü Bing

During strong winds and heavy rain, thick clouds often bring unusual objects with them. Falling from the sky, they create a strange spectacle. Historical records mention rain of fish, rain of insects, and rain of frogs, which may be true and not entirely fabricated. The reason is that ponds and ditches may contain these objects, which are then swept into the air by hurricanes, enveloped in clouds, and carried for hundreds of miles before falling with the raindrops, astonishing those who see them. There is nothing strange about it.

Recently, the sky over Paris rained red mud. On that day, thick clouds gathered, unusually dark. Suddenly, the clouds dispersed, and rain fell, with each drop being a reddish-brown slurry. Instantly, roads, vehicles, and buildings were covered, as if a team of painters had dyed the entire city of Paris. In some streets, the accumulated red mud was about half an inch high, an unprecedented sight.

Reportedly, the red mud that fell in Paris came from the Sahara Desert, 1,500 miles away. It was blown into the air in northern Africa, drifted north, crossed the Mediterranean Sea, and finally landed in Paris, creating this strange phenomenon.

Moreover, the books of Yang's Haiyuan Pavilion in Liaocheng have also been scattered and lost. The Song Dynasty editions of the collected works of Liu Zongyuan, Meng Haoran, and Meng Dongye were taken to Japan from Tianjin for 80,000 gold coins. One can imagine what else has been lost. This was one of the four great book collectors in the late Qing Dynasty, during the Daoguang and Xianfeng eras. Yet, his descendants could not preserve his collection. Although the losses were partly due to the chaos of war, those responsible for local culture cannot escape blame.

We have always lamented the burning of the Yongle Encyclopedia. Now, it is said that the British Library still holds over 80 volumes. How did they end up in Western hands? This raises many questions. Judging from this, the loss of our nation's ancient books is not merely a matter of neglecting them or letting them become dust. Even theft is tolerated, so that what was intended to promote national glory and embellish great undertakings must be begged from foreign countries decades later, seeking to pick up their scraps and feed them back to their motherland. Is this not truly sad and deplorable? Therefore, I bring this to the attention of the scholars of our nation.

Recording a Shanghai Prophet's Enlightenment – Jue Mi

▲ Today's Relocation of the Shanghai County Seat

▲ Predicted Twenty Years Ago

Zhu Cuifang, the former abbot of the western chamber of the Shanghai City God Temple, was a Taoist priest from Baoshan. His Taoist name was Yu Feng Daoren (Jade Peak Taoist). The Taoist was skilled in divination, and his predictions always came true. When Yuan Haiguan was the magistrate of Shanghai County, there was a severe drought. Despite banning slaughter and praying for rain, there was no rain. He consulted the Taoist, who predicted rain on a specific day and time. On that day, the sky remained clear, and the magistrate doubted the prediction. However, when the predicted time arrived, clouds gathered, and rain fell heavily, exactly as predicted. The magistrate presented him with a plaque praising his profound understanding of the Book of Changes. Later, when Yuan left office, the Taoist told people that Yuan would surely return. Years later, Yuan was appointed the circuit intendant of Songjiang, Songjiang, and Taicang, and indeed returned to Shanghai. The Taoist was a vegetarian, abstaining from meat and strong-smelling foods. He wore a Taoist cap and robe, appearing dignified, yet he was also carefree. Many scholars in the county associated with him, treating him as an equal. He was especially close to Zhu Zijun, a respected elder. The two would often visit teahouses to drink tea or taverns to get drunk. Before the Qing Dynasty banned opium, Shanghai was filled with opium dens. They would often lie on a couch in these dens. Although the Taoist was a recluse, he was not constrained by social conventions. When the Taoist went out, he often gave people a hint of what to expect. If the sky was clear with no clouds, showing no sign of rain, and the Taoist carried rain gear, then there would surely be a heavy downpour along the way. If the sky was overcast and showing no sign of clearing, and the Taoist did not carry an umbrella, then the rain would surely stop after he left. Sometimes, before going out, he would predict several things, and they would come true after he left. For example, if he said, "Going out today will bring minor setbacks and be wary of petty people," then there would surely be theft or loss of property that day. If he said, "Going out today will bring an unexpected encounter," then there would surely be an unexpected event that day. Sometimes, he would encounter something on the road and predict its future, and it would come true without fail. One day, while walking with Mr. Zijun, they saw a certain family building a temple. The Taoist sighed and said, "Although this temple is being built now, I fear that the day it is completed will be the day it is torn down." Mr. Zijun did not believe him at the time. However, later, when they passed by again, the temple was being torn down because it obstructed the road. One day, the Taoist was in an opium den, puffing away with several others. The den faced the city walls of Shanghai. He suddenly pointed at the city walls and said something extraordinary: "The city walls of Shanghai will soon be torn down." The even more extraordinary thing was that the Shanghai county seat would be relocated. This was probably during the late Guangxu era. People who heard this thought it was absurd and unbelievable. They did not believe it at all. After the revolution, the city walls were indeed torn down. Thus, the Taoist's prediction about the city walls came true. However, they still believed that the Taoist's prediction about the relocation of the Shanghai county seat would never come true. After the Shanghai county seat was reorganized into a municipality, those who had heard the Taoist's words believed that since Shanghai had been divided into a municipality and a county, the Shanghai county seat would surely be relocated as the Taoist had predicted. Now, the relocation is underway. Thus, the Taoist's prediction about the relocation of the Shanghai county seat has also come true. The Taoist passed away many years ago. When he made these predictions, it was over twenty years ago.

Brief Notes on Cooking – Zui Chi Sheng

In the art of eating, cleanliness and freshness are paramount. Then, with proper cooking and suitable combinations, the food will naturally be palatable, filling, and delicious. Even if Yi Ya were reborn, he would not go beyond this principle. Today, various regional restaurants in Shanghai are numerous, all claiming to employ famous chefs and emphasize cooking techniques. However, it is rare to find those that are truly excellent and flavorful. Often, lavish feasts are presented with novel designs, but upon closer inspection, one is left shaking one's head and frowning. There is no "value for money." This is simply because too much emphasis is placed on form, and the cooking is not up to par. Therefore, the problems can be summarized into the following three points, which I will discuss in detail below, hoping to contribute to improvement.

(1) Overuse of Seasonings

Things like "Ajinomoto" are used excessively, almost added to everything. I have seen cooks holding a bottle in one hand, sprinkling it arbitrarily, thus masking the true flavor. This creates a special artificial umami. Moreover, overuse of this substance can cause physical discomfort, such as dry mouth, thirst, and frequent bowel movements, as proven by many people with glucoseurea. This type of seasoning is meant to be used sparingly, so each bottle comes with a small ear-spoon-shaped spoon. The current excessive use defeats the purpose of the original creators.

(2) Lack of Freshness

Regardless of the item, everything is placed in the refrigerator. Although they may last longer, even if the fish isn't spoiled or the meat isn't rotten, the meat becomes stiff and loses its original flavor. What is the point of overusing seasonings then? Fish, in particular, should not be stored for too long. Those who greedily use cheap "refrigerated" products are even more despicable.

(3) Excessive Greasiness

Whether it's soup, stir-fries, clear stews, or braised dishes, they are often thickened with starch, and the oil spills everywhere. The food is both oily and greasy, easily causing aversion and indigestion.

The above three points are the most prominent and are highlighted here. Those involved in the food business should reform and correct these issues so that both enjoyment and hygiene can benefit. As a gluttonous person myself, I have high hopes.

European Travel Correspondence (98) – Liu Haisu

▲ Pilgrimage to Italy Diary

(Ten Days in Rome (21))

We lingered in the courtyards, halls, and chapels, seeing many standing, lying, crouching, leaning against the walls, or looking up into the sky—gray-haired old men, struggling youths, lively and arrogant heroes, serene and beautiful goddesses—countless stone statues left over from thousands of years ago. These are famous Greek and Roman sculptures. Among these statues, the full chests and agile limbs are the most striking. Other details are also vividly expressive. All physical forms and postures have reached the most vivid and perfect realm. Even today's most precise and successful researchers of the human body would probably be unable to match them. There are also countless elegant fragments everywhere, all imbued with abundant and fulfilling life. Each one has the power and desire to step down from its pedestal. They are the condensation of human life from ancient times. They not only allow the glory and greatness of the Vatican to endure in the world but also allow the creative spirit of the ancients to endure forever. Strive! Strive for the expression of life! I thoroughly enjoyed these treasures of the Vatican. At that moment, I truly felt as if I were traveling in the past of thousands of years ago, intoxicated by the blue sky and sunny beaches of the southern lands. I felt that the human soul is forever bathed in clear or sorrowful sunlight.

However, I should also honestly write about my actual feelings here. In this Vatican filled with countless ancient treasures, there are also many modern paintings and sculptures on display. Comparing the two, there is a great difference. Being among the two creates different feelings. In particular, the latter can make us feel dull and mentally weak. The sculptures are mostly imitations of Greek or Roman masterpieces, with only artificial muscles, exaggerated postures, and stiff hands and feet for us to see. The so-called artist's individuality and imagination have all disappeared. This is what I deeply regret. Superficially, they seem brave and exaggerated, displaying a fierce and predatory appearance, but they do not give me any comfort. Not only that, but their artificiality makes me want to vomit for ten days.

The lively models of athletic competitions of strong and healthy nudes from the past are no longer seen today. They no longer pursue their legacy, nor do they want to absorb new inspiration. They simply imitate those Greek and Roman archetypes, concerning themselves with dull techniques and fixed theoretical methods. Therefore, they only have repetitive imitations and exaggerated works. The works are filled with their calculating skills, with no great inspiration directly revealed. They cannot create, only imitate.

Commercial News

Financial Gold Market Turns Declining

▲ Seventeen and a Half Taels Slashed

▲ All-Day Wind, Fury, and Rain

Yesterday, February 10th, the gold market again trended downward, reversing the previous surge. However, the state was extremely confusing, as if mad and crazy. The raging waves were difficult to suppress. Throughout the day, there was a swing of twenty-two taels, causing widespread panic among traders. In the end, there was a sharp drop of more than two taels. Market trading was still active. In the morning session, Hengxing, Taikang, Dayi, Dade, Yuanxingyong, and others were buying, while sellers included Wanxing, Zhifengyongheng, Yu, and others. As for foreign exchange, it suddenly showed signs of decline, with posted rates remaining unchanged. This was likely because overseas silver markets were slightly lower, so there was no movement. Gold prices were weak early on. Later, various firms' cashiers differed, causing prices to rise and fall intermittently, fluctuating around eighty taels. The afternoon market was even more volatile. Taikang, Runyong, Fengyu, Da, and others were all buying, while Hengxing Tanfeng, Yongfuchang, and others were selling. Initially, the momentum was strong. The exchange rate once exceeded 790 taels. Drafts also showed profits. Afterwards, Indian money suddenly turned upward, and Shanghai's drafts turned loose and weak. In the fierce winds and heavy rain, the selling pressure in the market increased, almost to the point of decline. Suddenly, there was a drastic drop of twenty taels. People were fearful and anxious. Suddenly, the 770-tael level was broken. Such a market was like a floating duckweed, impossible to grasp. It is said that large traders will return to the market this morning.

▲ Seven Taels Down at Early Open

The March contract opened at 782 taels, down seven taels. Although large bars were down by one-eighth, silver prices did not change, and sentiment was immediately shaken. Subsequently, due to Dayi's purchase of a complete set, it rose by more than two taels to 84 taels and 70 cents. However, Fuchang, Yuanheng, Hengyu, and others came to sell, and banks mutually made spot deals first, causing 120,625 Taiwanese to buy Dalian at 1 tael 73 cents and 50 cents. The market was in a depressed state, plunging by about ten taels. By 9:10 AM, it was only 74 taels. Then, wheat firms absorbed three and four-month British gold at two pence, and Taikang, Runfu, Yu, and others bought, quickly recovering six or seven taels. When the telegraph price was announced, it was 81 taels, with posted rates remaining unchanged, slightly retreating to 79 taels and 50 cents. Before long, buyers became active, and by 9:45 AM, it was 82 taels and 80 cents. When Xinhneg and others sold, it retreated again to 79 taels. Around 10:00 AM, Hengxing, Taikang, Runfu, Fuchang, Yuanheng, and others rushed to buy, and British gold seemed firm. The March contract could be sold at 1 penny 937500, and at a quarter past ten, it had risen to 87 taels. Afterwards, Xinhneng, Hengyu, goods firms, and others had all sold, and the market turned downward. From 10:20 AM to 11:20 AM, there was a drop of more than six taels, with fluctuations of two or three taels up and down. Then, it was only 80 taels and 5 cents. After five or six minutes, it rose by more than three taels, reaching 84 taels, encouraging sellers. At 11:45 AM, it rose to 80 taels and 5 cents, and Hengxing and others bought again. At noon, it was 83 taels and a half. The closing price was 82 taels and 3 cents. Goods were still priced at 856 taels and 2 cents, a reduction of over seventy taels.

Afternoon Market Waves Frequently

The afternoon market opened at 82 and a half taels. Later, due to a drop of 12 annas in the Indian exchange rate, Taikang, Runyu, Da, Yongfeng, and others made aggressive advances, and prices gradually rose. Drafts were also good. Banks engaged in deals with three-month British gold at 1 penny 937500. Sumitomo absorbed spot Dalian at 1 tael 74 cents and 75 cents. By 3:00 PM, it reached 91 taels. Then, it turned weak because it was reported that the Indian exchange rate had suddenly recovered by 10 annas, especially as the Shanghai market suddenly loosened. Banks bought April and May British gold at 2 pence 0625 and then had difficulty selling. At 3:20 PM, it was 77 and a half taels. In just over ten minutes, it rose by more than four taels. After 2:30 PM, the storm suddenly arose. Zhifeng, Yongheng, Xingyuanmao, Shui, and others in the market all came to sell. So the March British gold 2 pence 125 could be settled. In one fell swoop, it was down twelve or thirteen taels. By 4:00 PM, it was suddenly 69 taels. Afterwards, short sellers slightly covered, and it was heard that banks were dealing with one-month British gold at 2 pence 115. Therefore, it rose by four taels to 71 taels. It was then suppressed again to 70 taels and 5 cents, and then again to 71 taels. It was quite complex and difficult to grasp. The market closed at 4:30 PM at 771 and a half taels, a sharp drop of 17 and a half taels compared to the previous day. However, after the close, it again traded around 70 taels. The largest price for the day was 91 taels, and the smallest price was 69 taels, a swing of twenty-two taels. Low priced goods early in the morning were 82 and a half taels, noon closing at 82 taels, afternoon at 83 and a half taels, and closing price at 70 taels. Prices were suppressed by seventy-one taels and four taels to sixty-five taels. Before registration, the morning market was seventy-seven taels to eighty-two taels, and the afternoon market was seventy-one taels to seventy-six taels, with water replenishment at seventy-seven taels in the morning and seventy-one taels in the afternoon.

Canceling Obstructions to Trade and Following Old Regulations

▲Market Overview: Currently, the silver dollar market is quiet due to few transactions. Generally, the market is dull, so there are no major events to record. However, because the period for settling accounts is approaching for both the silver and money industries, the final procedures are unusually troublesome, making collections and settlements particularly busy and the situation quite complicated.

▲Exchange Rates: The opening exchange rate for silver dollars was 7 qian 2 fen 1 li. The afternoon rate was 7 qian 2 fen 0 hao 8 hu 7 hu ban. The final rate was 2 hao ban lower than the bullish rate of the previous day (silver exchange rate). White loaning continued from the previous day. The morning and afternoon rates were both white loans with no interest. No extra money was added to the initial amount.

▲Subsidiary Coin Market Conditions: Jiangnan small silver dollars opened at 6 qian 7 fen 8 li in both the morning and afternoon, exactly the same as the previous day. There was no change in the afternoon rate. 6,000 jiao worth of transactions were made in the morning and 3,000 jiao in the afternoon. Guangdong small silver dollars opened at 6 qian 7 fen 5 li in the morning and 6 qian 7 fen 5 li 7 hao ban in the afternoon. 140,000 jiao worth of transactions were made in the morning and 120,000 jiao in the afternoon. Copper coins were reduced by 7,000 to 342,000 wen.

▲Silver Dollar Inflow and Outflow: (Silver) Yesterday, banks received and settled over 1.5 million in Hua Shang settlement bills, 2.56 million in foreign settlement bills, approximately 8 million in various commodity exchange taxes and other fees, over 4 million in settlement payments, 2 to 3 million in special funds and deposits, and 1.3 million withdrawn from the warehouse. Japanese banks received and settled over 3.7 million in various payments, over 600,000 in settlement payments, and 100,000 withdrawn from the warehouse. Money shops and silver firms received and settled over 4.11 million in single receipts, over 4.9 million in initial payment funds, over 1.1 million in remittances from various routes, and over 100,000 in cash. (Foreign currency) 1.69 million in exchange bills were made in the morning and 880,000 in the afternoon. 30,000 in banknotes were made in the morning and 25,000 in the afternoon. 184,000 in off-market banknotes were made in the morning and 125,000 in the afternoon. Bank transactions amounted to 600,000 in inter-bank trading in the morning and 500,000 in inter-bank trading in the afternoon. Over 1.8 million in foreign exchange settlements were made between foreign accounts at banks, and over 1.9 million in banknotes flowed in and out. Money shops and foreign firms received and settled over 4.8 million in single foreign currency receipts, over 2.2 million in foreign currency initial payment funds, and over 1.4 million in foreign currency loans.

Securities - Bond Prices Fluctuate

Yesterday, the transaction volume of various bonds in the local market totaled 62,000 yuan in spot transactions, including 34,000 yuan for First Customs bonds and 25,000 yuan for troop disbandment bonds. Other bonds were transacted at low volumes. The futures market remained stable. Market buying and selling were not quiet. The total volume for the morning and afternoon sessions combined was approximately 7 million yuan. The 20-year cigarette bonds and troop disbandment bonds were more active, reaching 1.6 to 1.7 million each. Reorganization and the 1910 and 1919 Customs bonds each reached over 800,000 yuan. Other bonds remained relatively stable. The supply and demand situation of various bonds was more balanced than before. Large investors remained in a wait-and-see attitude with no major buying or selling, so bond prices tended to be stable, fluctuating by only a few jiao in both the morning and afternoon sessions. The fluctuations were minimal compared to the previous day's mixed gains and losses. However, two-month financial bonds fell back by 8 jiao.

Cotton Yarn - Yarn Market More Moderate

The yarn market felt somewhat calm and confidence remained steady. Buyer attitudes were still firm. Fortunately, after an additional 20 taels of special margin were added, it was difficult for ordinary retail investors to make new transactions, so market conditions were more moderate. However, spot yarn business became increasingly quiet. Each group was only in the process of settling accounts, without any enthusiasm. Currently, most people think the exchange rate is high and their ambitions have reached their peak.

▲More New Human Bids, Gradually Fewer: The market opened with flat sentiment. Later, due to retail investors settling accounts and a lack of new buyers, the results were four, five, and six qian to one liang five or six qian for each route. In the afternoon, market conditions became tense again. Some bulls in the one-three market closed out positions, and the market turned looser. Each month fell by three, four, five, six, or nine qian to one liang. Total transaction volume for the day was 25,150 bales. Records show that Mei Ji sold 1,250 bales, Mingde 1,050 bales, Tianlong 1,150 bales, Yi Chang 1,300 bales, and Xin Cheng 1,350 bales. Geng Feng bought 1,650 bales, Shen Chang 1,400 bales, and Chang Feng 800 bales. Closing prices are recorded on the left.

Cotton Market Slightly Looser

Since an additional 10 taels of special margin were added to the cotton market, conditions have felt slightly more relaxed. Due to insufficient funds, it is difficult for retail investors to buy, so transactions have decreased and market conditions have become flat. However, buyer attitudes are still pulling tightly. Because foreign exchange rates are not loose and imported foreign cotton is still difficult to import at a reasonable price, bullish intentions are still strong. However, some manufacturers are selling. The future development depends on the shift in foreign exchange.

▲Many Han Bids Closing Positions: The Han bid market opened with tight sentiment due to the residual effects of the previous day. By the second and third rounds, because American cotton was flat and Indian cotton fell slightly, each month fell by three or four qian. In the afternoon, due to some bulls closing positions, each fell by four or six qian. Total transaction volume for the day was 75,400 dan. Grains - He Xia Rice Market Tightens

▲Zhabei: Yesterday, more than twenty sources arrived in Lili Road. Sales turned brisk because a few stores needed to build up inventory. Some cargo owners planned to sell it after settlement. As a result, the market became more active. North China white japonica rice and glutinous rice were bid up by one jiao. Special top-quality japonica rice was scarce and even more beautiful. Sheep japonica rice sales were strong and arrivals were weak, and the price also rose by nearly one chi. Du Jian and Bu Jian rice were stable. Demand from various parties was not smooth and there were few high-quality goods, so there were few transactions. The arrival of Bianyin Yuanlai rice continued. Wine sales were mediocre and retail sales were good, so prices were slightly firm. It is heard here that a plan to stop measuring in dou will be implemented from the 14th, so trading in both markets is turning brisk.

▲Hu Nan: Yesterday, there were not many arrivals from inland China. Sales on this street were uneven. Changxi japonica rice was particularly high-quality, so top-quality rice was welcomed by buyers. Ordinary medium-quality rice prices were stable. Su Tong white japonica rice sold well. Retail and village sales inquiries were good, and prices were firm by one jiao. South China glutinous rice arrivals and sales were balanced and prices were high and firm. Sheep japonica rice market conditions were brisk because inventory and arrivals were thin and Jiangsu customer rice was in demand by customer groups, so it was slightly affected and prices gradually became tight. Bianyuan Yinhua prices were slightly higher for those greedy to buy and more than half a chi above for those with less appetite.

Flour Market Wavering and Unstable

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in both the upper and lower markets, prices for each month saw an unstable situation. After the morning opening, because gold prices were still high and overseas wheat telegrams rose by six or seven jiao, some shorts were panicked and rushed to buy near-term and long-term contracts, each rising by two or three fen. Market sentiment was very strong, and it seemed that there would be a continuation of the gains from the previous day, but once prices rose, most of the floating bulls and inland bulls sold out in droves to take profits, so the market saw a reaction. The current month fell by a small amount of three fen, the next month fell by a small amount of four or five fen, and the long-term contracts all followed suit. Later, cotton yarn firms took the opportunity to actively enter the market, and the market was up again, but by the late period, gold prices fell slightly, so the July closing price fell by a small amount of two fen. February had no changes, the next month fell by a small amount of 7.5, April fell by a small amount of 1.75, May fell by a small amount of 1.5, and June fell by a small amount of 0.5.

Wheat Market Gradually Loosening

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat market in both the upper and lower markets, each month saw a gradual loosening. Although overseas wheat was reported to have risen, cotton yarn firms did not continue to enter the market. Most of the floating bulls and inland buyers closed out positions before settlement because prices were sufficient, so they sold in large quantities, and the downstream followed. At the closing, the current month fell by a small amount of two fen, the next month fell by a small amount of two fen, April fell by a small amount of two fen, May fell by a small amount of five fen, June fell by a small amount of two fen, July fell by a small amount of four fen. There was little inflow and outflow of spot wheat, and the inventory was about 10,000 bales, mainly from the Yangtze River and Jiangbei routes. Train goods accounted for a small minority.

Standard Yellow Soybeans and Bean Cakes Suddenly Plunge

▲Market Closed for Settlement Starting Today

▲Yellow Soybeans: Yesterday, soybean trading was good because both buyers and sellers were mostly closing positions. Because the exchange will be closed for settlement starting today, customer groups closed out most positions except for those preparing to collect cash. In addition, the Dalian telegram suddenly fell, the gold market reported weakness, and a few people who had made large profits due to the soaring soybean prices closed out their positions, so selling pressure was strong throughout the day. The current month fell slightly due to some covering transactions, but the long-term contracts fell to the same level as the closing price at the end of last week. The previous day's rise had a tendency to be artificially inflated. This kind of large rise and large fall is really rare and truly an unexpected change. The closing results were: February fell by 6 fen, March fell by 9 fen, April fell by 1 qian 1 fen, and May fell by 1 qian.

▲Bean Cakes: Yesterday, the bean cake market saw a sharp drop in raw materials and poor sentiment, which led to many floating bulls and new shorts selling in the morning and afternoon sessions. However, according to observations of the market sentiment on the previous day, there was a strong upward trend, so the morning opening still carried the residual momentum of the previous day and moved steadily. However, Dalian customer groups and foreign firms suddenly dumped large quantities, causing the market to fall with the general trend. At the closing, March and June both fell by 2 fen 2 li 5 hao, April fell by 3 fen, and May fell by 3 fen 5 hao.

Silk and Tea - Factory Filature in High Demand

The filature silk market is trending firmly because only 30-40% of silk factories in Shanghai are open, and only about 30 factories in Wuxi are operating. The production of filature silk is limited, while demand is still high, so supply cannot meet demand and prices are trending higher. Yesterday, Xin Fu imported 25 dan of superior filature silk, and the price had already risen to 194 liang.

Tea Market Increasingly Desolate

Yesterday, the various European firms' attitudes were negative because the telegrams sent last week had not been forwarded, and there were no transactions of Zhenmei pearl tea, etc. The entire market only saw Tongfu Foreign Firm buying 93 boxes of needle-shaped green tea, and the selling price was from 25 liang to 33 liang, with little change from the previous day.

Local News

Huang Shaoxiong Returned to Shanghai Yesterday

▲Resting Briefly Before Taking a Ship Back to Guangxi

Mr. Huang Shaoxiong previously went to Beijing at the summons of Chairman Chiang to discuss the aftermath of the Guangxi situation. A solution has now been agreed upon. The central government has internally decided to appoint Mr. Huang as the Director of Rehabilitation for Guangxi Province, with Wu Tingyang as the co-director, and Li Bai and Zhang Yu will go abroad for inspections under the guise of foreign study. The Guangxi affair has come to an end. Wu Tingyang returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday. Huang Shaoxiong and his wife arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 7:00 AM on the overnight express train from Beijing. They will rest briefly before taking a ship to Hong Kong to return to Guangxi.

Fan Qiwu to Return to Guangdong

▲Arrived in Shanghai from Beijing at 7:00 AM This Morning

▲Solution Agreed Upon for the 8th Route Army Expenses

Fan Qiwu, the Director of the Guangdong Department of Finance, came to Beijing to discuss the reorganization of Guangdong's finances and to negotiate the issue of the 8th Route Army's expenses with Minister of Finance Song Ziwen and General Commander of the 8th Route Army Chen Jitang. It is heard that a solution has been agreed upon. Mr. Fan is scheduled to return to Shanghai from Beijing this morning and will return to Guangdong with Chen Jitang in the coming days. Mr. Fan's wife already took the SS President Grant last night to return ahead of him.

Miller and Murphy Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

National Government advisor Mr. Miller and renowned New York architect Mr. Murphy arrived in Shanghai on the SS President Grant from the United States. They arrived at the dock at around 10:00 AM yesterday. Murphy is here to plan the construction project for Nanjing City and the central area of Greater Shanghai. He visited China once last year and drew up an outline for the construction of the capital. This is his second visit and it is expected he will have a detailed design.

South Manchurian Japanese Commercial Delegation Arrives in Shanghai

▲Develop Trade with China

In order to develop its trade, the various commercial sectors of South Manchuria, initiated by the Japanese businesses in Dalian, Fengtian, Lushun, Anshan, Fushun, Andong, Tieling, Changchun, Harbin, and Gongzhuling, organized the Shanghai Commercial Conditions Observation Delegation. Led by Kamisari Kogichi, the Director of the Manchurian Import Association Federation, the delegation consists of 84 representatives from various industries, who have come to Shanghai to observe. The delegates have already arrived in Shanghai on the Japanese ship Changchun Maru and are staying at the Banzai Hotel in Hongkou. After observing market conditions in Shanghai, they are scheduled to visit the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce tomorrow, and then return to Manchuria. [Image of Chen Xizeng]

It is heard that there will be no ceremony today, only a meeting with the staff and instructions for deployment. Various Industry Tax Research Association Received Letters and Telegrams Yesterday

The Various Industry Tax Research Association of this city, which telegraphed the National Government Executive Yuan and the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provincial Governments that the amount of business tax in each province should be based on the loss of the 25% surtax on land tax in each province, received the following letters and telegrams yesterday: (1) The letter from the National Government Civil Affairs Office stated, "Dear Sir, the President's Office forwarded your association's telegram regarding the Zhejiang Provincial Government's business tax, which should be limited to 1.4 million, and requested special consideration. The President has instructed the Executive Yuan, etc., so we are forwarding this letter for your information." (2) The telegram from the Zhejiang Provincial Government stated, "To the Various Industry Trade Association Tax Research Committee of Shanghai, we have received your telegram, and the Department of Finance has been ordered to investigate and handle it. Special reply, Zhejiang Provincial Government seal."

Official Correspondence Regarding Business Taxes by Various Industries

▲Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Requests Tax Exemption

The Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Weaving Association sent a telegram yesterday to the National Government Council and Ministries, addressed to President Hu of the Legislative Yuan of the National Government, Minister of Finance Song, and Minister of Industry Kong, saying: "We respectfully note that the Finance Ministry's resolution from last year's abolition of lijin (transit tax) conference stipulated the principle of 'one item, one tax.' Goods already subject to special central taxes should not be subject to business tax again, to reduce complications and avoid disturbing businesses. This law is well-intentioned and beneficial. However, we now hear that various provinces collecting business tax still include domestically produced silk fabrics. The industries of both provinces are deeply alarmed, and have come to the association to strongly appeal. Silk fabrics are already subject to special consumption tax, and cannot bear the additional burden of business tax, lest they fall back into shackles after barely escaping the lijin system. Surely the esteemed officials who care for our compatriots and cherish our resources would not bear to allow this to happen. This is our first request. Furthermore, the increased import duties were originally intended to compensate for the loss from abolishing lijin. However, we have heard that the customs report after increasing import duties shows that the increased revenue is more than sufficient to compensate. It seems unnecessary to further burden domestic goods with taxes, repeating the previous mistake. This is our second request. Therefore, after deliberation by the representatives of the silk industry associations of various counties in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces under our association, we respectfully submit this request to the government, asking it to order the governments of various provinces to exempt the silk industry from business tax, thereby saving domestic silk and benefiting industry and commerce. We respectfully submit this telegram and request that your council and ministries investigate and implement, and await your instructions with utmost respect. This is truly beneficial for the Party. The Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Weaving Association respectfully bows."

▲Silk Fabric Industry Requests Tax Reduction

The Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai Silk Fabric Trade Association sent a telegram yesterday to the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and the Shanghai Municipal Government, saying: "We respectfully address the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments and the Shanghai Municipal Government. The proposed business tax rate for silk fabrics by the provincial governments is excessively high, not only placing an unbearable burden on merchants but also posing the greatest obstacle to promoting domestically produced silk fabrics. The association's members have dispatched representatives to the central and provincial governments to plead their case and express their grievances, which have been sympathetically received. We now hear that Zhejiang province intends to implement a uniform tax across the province starting March 1st, and Jiangsu province will likely follow soon. However, we have not yet received clear instructions regarding the reduction of silk fabric tax rates. Merchants are alarmed and eagerly await your response. Therefore, the association has again decided to telegraph your governments, urging you to consider the livelihood of the people, heed the concerns of businesses, recognize that silk fabrics are daily necessities for the people, and that the silk industry is the source of livelihood for farmers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. All business tax rates should adhere to the guidelines issued by the ministry, not exceeding two per thousand, and should be levied on the business itself, not based on the type of goods, to avoid excessive disruption. We earnestly request that your governments make a timely decision and promptly issue clear instructions to reassure the anxious and prevent further anticipation. The Preparatory Committee of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai Silk Fabric Trade Association respectfully bows, Ash."

▲Seafood Industry Requests Tax Reduction

The Shanghai Seafood and Sundries Trade Association sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, saying: "Respectfully, we have examined the regulations promulgated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government for the collection of business tax. The tax rates all exceed those stipulated by the ministry, in some cases by more than ten times. Moreover, there are errors and misunderstandings. For example, our industry, which is entirely the seafood and sundries industry, is labeled with 'ginseng and bird's nest,' and is classified as a luxury item, taxed at ten per thousand. Ginseng and bird's nest are in the ginseng and bird's nest industry, and seafood and sundries are in the seafood and sundries industry. They are clearly distinct and cannot be equated. Furthermore, the goods we deal in, except for shark fins which are slightly expensive, are all ordinary food items, and many are necessities for the poor. For example, seaweed and kelp, vegetable reds, jellyfish skin, glass noodles, arrowroot powder, dried fish, and sago rice, cost only four or five taels to eight or nine taels per dan, and are mostly sold to poor households in the north and south. If these are classified as luxury items and subjected to the same heavy tax, at a time when the poor are losing their jobs and struggling to survive, our industry will hardly survive, and the common people will be in an even more precarious situation. The above only addresses one aspect of the error. As for the meaning of business tax, it was originally intended to compensate for the cost of local administration after the abolition of lijin. Since this city has not suffered losses from the abolition of lijin, it should not follow the example of other provinces and increase the burden on the people. Moreover, the ministerial regulations stipulate that business tax, regardless of the item, should not exceed two per thousand, and there is no classification by category. How can the Jiangsu Provincial Government disregard this and disregard the authority of the central government, and violate the central government's intention to eliminate malpractices and benefit our people? Our industry is deeply concerned about its survival and has no choice but to appeal to your association to forward this to the central government and the ministries, urging the Jiangsu Provincial Government to revise the regulations and allow the business tax to be collected according to the ministry's regulations, regardless of the industry, generally at a rate of one per thousand or less, to alleviate the difficulties of businesses by relying on government orders. This would be truly beneficial for all."

Difficulty in Exempting the Book Industry from Business Tax

▲City Chamber of Commerce Receives Reply from Ministry of Finance

The City Chamber of Commerce previously received a petition from the Book Industry Association, requesting exemption from business tax due to the book industry's relationship with culture. After forwarding the telegram to the Ministry of Finance, it received the following reply from the Ministry of Finance: "To the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, we have received your telegram. We have investigated this case and found that the association previously submitted a petition directly to the ministry, which was批示 (approved/commented): 'We have reviewed the recent Administrative Yuan approved general guidelines for provincial business taxes and supplementary measures. The shops that should be exempt from business tax are limited to those that have already paid income tax or special taxes to the central government, as well as banks and special companies. The book industry belongs to the printing and publishing industry, and its business tax should be collected according to regulations. The request to issue a notice to exempt all provinces is difficult to approve,' etc., printed and filed. You are hereby notified, Finance Ministry Seal."

Ministry's Response to Request for Supporting the Cigarette Industry

▲Difficult to Approve

The Ministry of Finance replied yesterday to the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce's telegram, which pleaded for permission to allocate bonuses from the collection of the consolidated cigarette tax, in accordance with the reward and protection measures stipulated in the general guidelines for special consumption taxes, to support the cigarette industry. The reply stated that according to the telegram from漾日, and the telegram of the same date from the Administrative Yuan to the chamber of commerce regarding the same matter, "We have investigated and found that cigarettes are a luxury item and not an item that must be rewarded and protected. Furthermore, the revenue from this consolidated tax has been designated by the National Government as a fund for issuing treasury bonds, which concerns the credit of national debt and should not be used arbitrarily. The request to allocate reward bonuses is difficult to approve. You are hereby notified." This is the reply.

Diplomatic Discussion Committee to Hold Regular Meeting

▲Tang Liu Reports on the Situation of Overseas Chinese in Singapore

The Diplomatic Discussion Committee of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will hold its 34th regular meeting on the 12th. It is reported that the agenda includes a draft proposal to be submitted to the ministry regarding the water supply issue in the public concession, as well as proposals to request the authorities to actively prepare for passport checks for foreigners entering the country, and other important cases. In addition, Mr. Tang Liu, former Consul-General in Singapore and a member of the committee, who recently returned to the country, will report on the situation of overseas Chinese in Singapore.

Protecting the Public's Payment of Grain Tax

▲Police Protection Assigned by City and County

Since the division of Shanghai City and County, the grain counters for collecting busy cao grain tax remain next to the county government. Now, the city's Land Bureau believes that the current period is the peak season for the people to pay the winter grain tax, and the next few days will be particularly busy. Fearing that bandits might seize the opportunity to rob the counters, in addition to sending a letter to the Public Security Bureau to instruct the relevant second district and second precinct to dispatch police to protect the counters in shifts, the county Public Security Bureau chief police will also assist in the protection.

Overcrowding for Exchanging Housing Tax for City Public Bonds

▲Request to Add Staff at the Finance Bureau

The municipal government previously borrowed housing tax for its use. Starting this month, it began exchanging it for 19-year customs treasury bonds and city public bonds, which has been announced in the newspaper. It is reported that recently, there has been extreme overcrowding for exchanging these treasury bonds. Those holding tickets have even had to wait from morning to night without receiving a notification. It is expected that someone will send a letter to the Municipal Finance Bureau, requesting that it find a way to add staff to handle this matter, to avoid wasting time and facilitate convenience.

National Treasury Has No Funds to Subsidize the Decline of Sichuan Silk

▲Ministry of Industry and Commerce Orders the National Federation of Commerce to Take Note

The National Federation of Commerce yesterday received an instruction from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, stating: "For your information, we have received a consultation from the Ministry of Finance, stating that it has received a letter from the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan, stating that President Jiang (Chiang Kai-shek) of the National Government has assigned the National Federation of Commerce's report on the decline of Sichuan silk, requesting the allocation of funds for relief and asking for tax exemptions to maintain it, to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for review. Although the current treasury funds are tight, Sichuan silk urgently needs to be maintained, which is also a real situation concerning finance. We are consulting you for review and reply. We have approved this consultation. If we are capable, we should allocate funds for relief. However, the national treasury currently has no funds for subsidies. We hereby reply for your information," etc. We have approved this. In the past, the association came to report and the Executive Yuan assigned it to our ministry, which was then consulted with the Ministry of Finance. With the approval of the previous consultation, we will now issue an order for your information, etc. The National Federation of Commerce has already informed the Sichuan silk merchant representative Li Kui'an and others to take note.

Shanghai County Government Meeting

The Shanghai County Government held its 56th county government meeting at 2 p.m. the day before yesterday. The attendees included County Magistrate Yan Yiyu, Finance Bureau Chief Wang Li, Construction Bureau Chief Wu Wenhua, Education Bureau Chief Shi She, Public Security Bureau Representative Chen Guozhen, County Secretary Ye Dezhen, and Second Section Chief Yu Fen. County Magistrate Yan served as chairman, and Hu Gongshou recorded the minutes. After performing the customary procedures, the chairman reported on the progress of the county Education Bureau in handling the public schools of the county's agencies. Then, discussions began, and it was resolved: (1) The county government's submission for discussion: how to use the remaining funds from the first session of public schools of the county's agencies. It was resolved that the Education Bureau would purchase items to reward the teachers. (2) The county government's submission for discussion: the date of this year's tree planting campaign is approaching, and where should the location be? It was resolved that the location of the new county government has not yet been fully determined, and the previous resolution is difficult to implement. The North Huipu Road project will be completed soon, so it is proposed to plant trees on North Huipu Road. The cost of the seedlings needed for tree planting on North Huipu Road will be paid from the North Huipu Road project funds. The remaining expenses for meetings and publicity will be handled according to the original plan. The meeting adjourned at 4 p.m.

Navy's Ma Jiang Aircraft Manufacturing Plant to Move to Shanghai

▲Shanghai Aircraft Division to Expand Seaplane Base

The Navy Aircraft Division, after deciding to expand into a seaplane base, plans to convert the old Navy warehouses near the West Battery, which used to store military equipment, into a Navy aircraft manufacturing plant. The base of the plant will move the aircraft manufacturing plant from Ma Jiang to Shanghai. Yesterday, Wang Chongheng, an engineer from the Aircraft Division, ordered craftsmen to repair the old warehouses at the West Battery. It must be completed by the end of this month. The Ma Jiang manufacturing plant has been instructed by Director Wang Zhu and Deputy Director Zeng Yijing to have the staff prepare for shipment next month. It is reported that the plant has more than one hundred craftsmen, and five aircraft, including the Hai Biao, Hai Diao, and Hai Yuan, which have been completed or are under construction, will also be brought to Shanghai together.

Special News from the Shipping Industry

▲Inland Small Steamers Will Not Operate Starting Tomorrow

▲Changfu Maru Runs Aground

The European liner Changfu Maru of the Japanese Kawasaki Steamship Company, which transported a large batch of hardware from Germany and the Netherlands to Shanghai this time, received a radio message from the ship yesterday, stating that the ship encountered fog at sea east of Australia, and the hull accidentally ran aground on a reef. The middle cabin has been breached, and seawater has entered. The situation is quite dangerous. The Kawasaki management office in Australia has sent a ship to rescue it. It is difficult to predict whether it can be safe and sound at this time.

▲Yichang Wheel Towed to Shanghai

The Yichang Maru wheel of the Jiangda Company on the Yangtze River encountered fog and ran aground at Yaojiagang, Tongzhou. The ship's horn was damaged, and the cargo hold was flooded. Passengers transferred to another wheel to Shanghai. The newspaper reported on this. The company sent the Jardine Matheson Victoria wheel to tow it, and it was towed to Wusong at 2:50 p.m. yesterday. It then drove into Shanghai and stopped at Hongkou. First, unload the cargo, and then enter the dock for major repairs.

▲Jiangda Rescue Again

Taigoo barge hit Jiangda's bow. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company sent six ironworkers to Dashengguan to tighten the two wheel bows that were broken, so as to be towed to Shanghai for repairs. Yesterday, the Shanghai Bureau received another telegram from Jiangda, saying that the Tunan wheel had been waiting at the mouth of Wujiang twice yesterday for the ironworkers to remove the barge, and then towed it to Shanghai for major repairs to the damaged keel and broken bow cabin in the factory.

▲Inland Wheels Stop Running

The old customs of the local inland shipping bureau cannot be avoided at the end of the lunar year. The export goods of various Shanghai merchants to various inland villages will be suspended from loading and unloading from the 7th and 8th of this month. This is because the Hakkas are closing their accounts and will no longer be in business. Inland small wheels, such as those on the Suzhou, Hangzhou, Xichang, and Hu lines, except for the China Merchants Bureau wheel, which is under the jurisdiction of the Construction Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, abide by the new calendar and are not allowed to stop navigation. Other commercially operated small wheels will have their last schedule today and will all stop running tomorrow.

Pacific American Wheel Expansion

▲Weihai Wheel Also Allowed to Join the Association

Wheel companies are competing to build new ships for the Pacific route and are doing their best to seek development in China. Japan Post, Changxing, etc. have built new wheels and entered the Sino-American line. The voyage speed has increased, and the amount of ship load has increased. The sea route has been shortened, and the faster the better. Now, the American merchant Dalai Ocean Bank has specially built two new wheels with 16 million US dollars and joined the Pacific Ocean. It can be opened in August and September of this year. The bank must add to the voyage due to business expansion. The method will be recorded as follows:

▲Add Panama Shuttle

The bank's Pacific wheel has two original lines, one to San Francisco and one to Seattle. After arriving in Shanghai, the two postal ships exchanged voyages, hence the name horseshoe route. This year, due to the completion of the new giant wheel, and the addition of three ships, the Longtian, Asami, and Chichibu, in the San Francisco class, the business has inevitably diminished. Lao Dalai decided to extend the sea voyage of the five Pacific postal ships to San Francisco and add the Panama to New York class. This can save the transportation of goods from Shanghai to the United States from the transfer of trains in San Francisco and pay huge freight charges. The president wheels, such as Cleveland, Bias, Huierxun, and Grant, which traveled between Jinshan and Shanghai, will start operating this new route from Panama to New York, starting with the Jackson wheel leaving Shanghai on April 3. It only takes 35 days from Shanghai to New York. Hu Xing has changed the schedule yesterday.

▲Two New Giant Wheels Added

The newly built Hoover and Coolidge, two president wheels, each with 33,800 tons of displacement, are unprecedented giant wheels in the Pacific Ocean. It has also been agreed that when the two new ships open in August and October of this year, they will also be assigned to this San Francisco to New York direct flight, so that the transportation of Chinese silk and tea to the United States can be spared the trouble of sea and land transit. It only takes 31 days to arrive. The ship is equipped with airplanes to pick up passengers, and there are cars that can go directly to the ship. It is the newest style postal ship in the Far East.

▲Expand the World Shuttle

The bank's World Shuttle originally had seven ships. Later, due to the addition of the Qiangsheng Wheel, the Hays and Monroe President Wheels were changed to the Singapore to New York line. Now, the Singapore side has expanded its ships to seven due to the start of business. When the Pacific wheel is greatly expanded, it is decided to add two more ships to the World Wheel, that is, the Hays and Monroe ships will be withdrawn from Nanyang and added to the World Road. In the future, there will be one wheel leaving the Pacific Ocean every day, and one ship will depart from the World Line every fourteen days.

▲Weihai Ship Joins the Association

Last year, the Weihai wheels of Shunheng and Tianjin, two banks in the Sino-American class, had a total of eleven ships, all of which were newly added to the Pacific Ocean, and competed with British, Japanese, and American merchants in the Far East shipping industry, resulting in a drop in water feet and a mess in freight rates. As a result, both sides were damaged. Now, after the British, Japanese, and American wheel companies consulted with the Weihai shipping company, they persuaded it to join the association and stop abusing the rate of decline. The Weihai Wheel Company has accepted and will be allowed to join the Pacific Water Foot Association starting next month and can open and load Huasi for export.

Reactions to the Opium Monopoly

▲Expressing Complete Resistance

Recently, there have been rumors that the tobacco control authorities have adopted an opium monopoly plan. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has collected reports from all parties and sent a letter to the authorities for attention. The details have been recorded in the previous report. It is reported that public groups in various places have paid special attention to the rumors of the opium monopoly. For example, the Chinese Medical Association and the Taxpayer Chinese Association in this city have sent letters to the association expressing their unanimous opposition and striving to achieve a thorough policy of prohibition. In addition, the Shanghai Christian Preaching Federation also sent a letter to the association, stating that through the standing committee of the Preaching Federation, the whole body unanimously advocated the thorough implementation of the complete prohibition policy and opposed the malpractices of monopoly. A meeting of all Christians will be called to resist. Other groups, such as the Zhejiang National Anti-Drug Branch, the Tianjin National Anti-Drug Branch Preparatory Office, the Harbin National Anti-Drug Branch, and the Fujian Poison Removal General Society, have all sent telegrams to the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association expressing their unanimous opposition, saying: (1) Opium is a public factory of public opinion. The prime minister's legacy is obvious. Opium's public sale is absolutely wrong to implement. (2) The government clearly ordered the prohibition of opium in the past, but now it sells it publicly in the future. It will surely be ridiculed by all countries. The international status and reputation will be unimaginable. How can we comfort the people and respond to the international community? (3) In addition to requesting the government to implement the prime minister's prohibition policy on the one hand and make a clear announcement to dispel doubts, we will convene a national anti-smoking conference as soon as possible to vigorously prohibit smoking. (4) Absolutely be the backing, hoping to actively oppose. It is reported that there are many other groups that have expressed unanimous opposition, and the association is collecting and publishing them one after another.

Postal Workers' Union Requests Housing Allowance

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union submitted a document to the Post Office Headquarters, stating: "The document is for Shanghai's high rents and difficult living conditions. Please take into account the situation and add a housing allowance of ten yuan to provide relief and comfort the public. According to the requirements of members of various branches, Shanghai is a major trading port with the largest number of residents, and rents are several times higher than in other parts of the interior. Postal workers who serve in Shanghai are mostly families, and their residence is even more difficult. Rents in areas with convenient transportation are not less than dozens of yuan, and those in remote areas may be slightly cheaper, but the daily transportation costs are even more expensive. Since last year, life in Shanghai has become increasingly difficult, and housing rents have more than doubled in the past. The postal workers feel the difficulty of making a living on the one hand, and the difficulty of living on the other hand. The pain is conceivable. The capital post office has been implementing the housing allowance for postal workers for many years, and there are also housing allowances and coal allowances in Harbin and other places for Shanghai's supply service. This is to avoid our postal workers from falling into a desperate situation due to facilities in the mainland. Even postal chiefs and others who enjoy high salaries have housing allowances and other allowances. Our Shanghai postal workers have small salaries and huge expenses. It is not enough to maintain if a housing allowance is not given separately. Therefore, we respectfully request that your bureau take into account the situation and add a monthly housing allowance of ten yuan to each level of employees from postal workers and below, to provide relief and comfort the public. I respectfully request approval, promulgation and implementation. I am overwhelmed by the urgency to wait for the order." (Hua Dong News Agency)

Fine Arts Workers' Dispute Mediation Successful

▲Supplementary Signature Today

The All-Factory workers of the Jingyi Leather Factory on Yokohama Road, Zhabei, and the Baziqiao Branch requested the payment of year-end bonuses for last year. The union dispatched personnel to discuss with the factory owner Zhou Wenlin without results. They continued to demand an increase in wages of seven yuan per person per month. The capital side had previously increased wages when rice prices soared in February last year, and it has been very considerate to the capital side without reducing wages now that rice prices have eased, so it was not allowed. Later, the capital side saw that the capital side did not respond, and immediately began to work slowly from the 7th. Seeing this, the capital side submitted a request to the Social Affairs Bureau for verification. In order to avoid the expansion of labor tides, the bureau dispatched Wang Bing to persuade and obtain the consent of both labor and capital to determine four methods: (1) Tian factory pays 15 days of wages per person as last year's bonus. (2) All workers will immediately restore the original work. (3) During the slack period, the work will be done by the labor side. (4) The request to increase wages will be submitted by the labor side to the party and government organs for verification, and it is scheduled to be 9 a.m. today. Both labor and capital parties will send representatives to the Social Affairs Bureau to formally supplement the signature.

Xialun Silk Factory Labor Tide Resolved

▲Signing of Seven-Item Agreement

The workers of the Xialun Silk Weaving Factory on Nanshan Road, Zhabei, in this city, proposed to improve the treatment because the factory's treatment was not good and the working hours were as long as 15 hours. The capital side ignored it, which led to a strike by all the workers on the 28th of last month. At the same time, they requested assistance from the Social Affairs Bureau. At 1 p.m. yesterday, the bureau called for mediation of this case. Bao Jinshi and Chen Baoshu, representatives of the capital side, and Chen Zhangru and Yang Dezhou, representatives of the labor side, agreed to sign the agreement with Wang Bing as the chairman. The seven agreements are as follows: (1) The deposit foreign funds deducted by the factory will be fully released, but the labor side must find a guarantor to guarantee to the factory that if the worker leaves the factory halfway during the school year without the factory's consent, the guarantor will compensate the deposit foreign funds of 50 yuan. (2) The daily working time shall not exceed twelve hours at most. If the factory opens night work, it must first obtain the consent of the workers. (3) The period of use of electric light bulbs is limited to one month as usual. (4) There are two holidays per month, one day each time. (5) Wages will be paid one day before the holiday. (6) Workers' food, the factory must strictly injure the kitchen and must not be too bad. (7) From today, all workers must work as usual, and the chairman announced the mediation was established.

to undertake commissions from industry and commerce to solve problems, analyze difficulties, and imitate or innovate, it has been greatly praised by various industries, who have vied to make use of its services, resulting in remarkable achievements.
